elsevier ltdepigenetic mechanisms comprise all those phenomena that influence chromatin structure and gene expression without modifying the sequence of the dna . dna methylation and hydroxymethylation are modifications that pertain a single base of the dna , . the cytosine ( ) . while dna methylation has been extensively studied and its effects on gene expression demonstrated in relation to several genes , dna hydroxymetilation has been recently described and the mechanisms of regulation have not been fully elucidated . histone modifications ( ) are the modification of the aminoacids in the histone tails that can be acetylated , methylated , adp-ribosylated , ubiquitinated , and phosphorylated . the modifications of specific residues of the histones , in particular through acetylation and methylation , determine conformational changes in the chromatin , a phenomenon known as chromatin remodeling ( ) . the small non coding rnas , and in particular micrornas ( mirnas ) , have been recently recognized as epigenetic mechanisms for its capacity to modulate the expression of specific genes . the mirnas are encoded by mirna genes and the transcripts are then modified in the cytosol to produce the mature mirnas that regulate specific target mrnas ( ) . fig . 1 . one-carbon metabolism provides the methyl groups for biological methylation reactions and for nucleotide synthesis . several nutrients actively influence the pathway : folate , involved in the delivery of methyl groups ; vitamin b6 , coenzyme of serine hydroxymethyltransferase ( shmt ) ; vitamin b2 , coenzyme of methylenetetrahydrofolate reductase ( mthfr ) ; vitamin b12 , coenzyme of methionine synthase ( ms ) ; several aminoacids such as methionine that is critical for the synthesis of s-adenosylmethionine ( sadomet ) , the universal methyl-donor for biological methylation reactions . fig . 2one-carbon metabolism nutrients known to influence epigenetic mechanisms . table 1epigenetic mechanismone-carbon metabolism nutrientsstudy detailsreferencesdna methylationfolatefolate-deficient diet was associated to genomic h

delim
elsevier ireland ltdepigenetic modifications of chromatin structure : different epigenetic modifications in chromatin during transcriptionally active and inactive state . dm ( demethylase ) , dnmt ( dna methyltransferase ) , hat ( histone acetyl transferase ) , hdac ( histone deacetylase ) , hmt ( histone methyltransferase ) . epigenetics and dcm : putative pathways and their candidate genes involved in pathophysiology of diabetic cardiomyopathy ( dcm ) . rectangular boxes show the genes which have shown to be epigenetically modulated in other diseases . et-1 , endothelin 1 ; f . a . , fatty acid ; ros , reactive oxygen species ; age , advanced glycation end products ; mhc , myosin heavy chain ; at1r , angiotenin1 receptor ; gult , glucose transporter ; serca , sarcoplasmic reticulum ca-atpase ; col4 , collagen type iv ; ppar , peroxisome proliferator activated receptor ; raas , renin – angiotensin aldosterone system ; hif , hypoxia inducing factor ; vegf , vascular endothelial growth factor and tgf , transforming growth factor . ⁎ . tel . : + 91 9316131057 ; fax : + 91 1722744401 . cardiovascular complications are a chief cause of mortality and morbidity in diabetic patients . recent studies suggest that epigenetic changes which may arise as a consequence of environmental factors play an important role in predisposition to disease . epigenetic mechanisms such as dna methylation , chromatin remodeling and histone modifications regulate the gene expression in response to environmental signals . role of epigenetics has been recognized in the pathology of diabetes , however its role in diabetic associated cardiomyopathy remains largely unexplored . in this article , we review current literature on the epigenetic mechanisms involved in diabetes and discuss recent evidence of epigenetic changes that may play an important role in pathophysiology of dcm . diabetes is the most common modifiable risk factor , and is a significant contributor to death

delim
elsevier b . v . molecular mechanisms through which hypoxia regulates histone methylation and gene expression ( ) in normoxia , hif-α is hydroxylated by phd enzymes at its proline residues and is subsequently subjected to vhl-mediated ubiquitination and proteasomal degradation . additionally , asparagine hydroxylation by fih blocks hif-α recruitment of cbp / p300 coactivators . under hypoxia , hif-α is stabilized and translocated to the nucleus , where it dimerizes with hif-β to induce the expression of histone-modifying enzyme genes with hre sequences . ( ) phd1 destabilizes histone methyltransferase g9a through proline hydroxylation and the vhl-driven ubiquitin-proteasome pathway . fih hydroxylates g9a and glp at asparagine residues to inhibit their methyltransferase activities . in hypoxia , g9a and glp are activated and repress a subset of anti-metastatic genes by adding h3k9me2 / 3 marks . ( ) the histone demethylases kdm5a and kdm6a are activated to demethylate h3k4 and h3k27 , respectively , in an oxygen-dependent manner . under hypoxia , they are inactivated , and gene expression is readjusted to cope with hypoxia . fig . 1hif-induced oncogenic histone modifiers in the cancer . a group of hif-induced histone modifiers ( kdm3a , kdm4b , kdm4c , kdm7b , and ezh2 ) epigenetically activate oncogenes that promote cancer progression in a hypoxic microenvironment . conversely , kdm5b promotes cancer progression by repressing tumor suppressor genes . nsclc , non-small-cell lung carcinoma . fig . 2hypoxia-responsive histone methyltransferases and demethylases . table 1categorynamealiaseshistone targetsexpression in hypoxiaactivity in hypoxiag

delim
elsevier ltdschematic depicts the epigenetics modifications in the development of organ fibrosis . micro-repetitive injuries caused by the external stimuli such as environmental stress , chemical drugs may alter gene expression through epigenetic mechanisms . epigenetic modifications include dna methylation , histone post translational modifications , chromatin remodeling complexes and non-coding rnas . several studies have demonstrated that these altered epigenetic modifications lead to aberrant expression of genes related to myofibroblast proliferation and differentiation — involved in the development and progression of organ fibrosis . fig . 1an overview of the atp-dependent chromatin remodeling complexes . ( a ) iswi and chd remodeling complexes are involved in the spacing of nucleosome . ( b ) swi / snf remodeling complexes are involved in the nucleosome ejection and sliding . ( c ) ino80 remodeling complexes are involved in the histone editing . iswi , imitation switch ; chd , chromodomain helicase dna ; swi / snf , switch / sucrose non-fermentable ; ino80 , inositol requiring mutant 80 . fig . 2epigenetic drugs that have entered clinical trials in the context of fibrotic diseases . table 1compoundmode of actioncompanyphasediseasenct identifiernicotinamideco-factor for sirt actionuniversity of colorado , denverphase iikidney diseasenct04040959nicotinamideco-factor for sirt actionmedice arzneimittel pütter gmbh & co kgphase iichronic kidney diseasenct01200784nicotinamideco-factor for sirt actionbeth israel deaconess medical centerphase iacute kidney injurynct02701127nicotinamideco-factor for sirt actionmayo clinicphase iiacute kidney injurynct04342975valproic acidhdac inhibitoruniversity hospital brusselphase ii / phase iiiidiopathic nephrotic syndrome

the domain architecture of the evolutionary conserved methyl-binder subunit of major classes of cd proteins in human genome . each protein contains a distinctive cd structural fold that is shown with corresponding amino acid numbers . chd superfamily of proteins harbour two tandem cds represented as cd1 and cd2 . hp1 isoforms in human : cbx1 , cbx3 and cbx5 consists of a csd along with the consensus cd . csd is situated at the c-terminus of cd region in hp1 isoforms . pc homologs : cbx2 , cbx4 , cbx6 , cbx7 and cbx8 harbours a single cd located at their n-terminus . cd regions in four cdy isoforms , two kmts : suv39h1 and suv39h2 , kat8 , msl3 and dcaf1 are represented . other specific domains for various chromatin functions are not shown . illustrated domains are in scale with the size of the proteins . fig . 1structure-based sequence alignment and organization of the cds . amino acid numbers of first and last residue in the alignment are noted . tandem cd1-cd2 from chd proteins and csd from hp1 isoforms are aligned independently . aromatic cage residues that recognize methylated lysines are in purple and shown with asterisks below . well conserved aromatic residues outside cage regions forms a complementary surface facilitating methyl-recognition are highlighted in purple and colon . conserved positive and negative charged residues are indicated as blue and red . black dots indicated the family specific conserved residues . fig . 2unrooted phylogenetic tree of cds and chromo barrel domains . the sequence alignment was used to construct the phylogenetic map of cd containing proteins . fig . 3mutation map of chromodomain-containing proteins in major tumor types . each dot represents the mutation in a single protein with respect to the tumor type . the multiple mutations in each protein corresponding single cancer type are indicated by # mark along with numbers . missense mutations are shown in red . description of cancer type is indicated as : aml-acute myeloid leukemia , acc-adrenocortical carcinoma , buc-bladder urothelial carcinoma , bic-breast invasive carcinoma , bidc-breast invasive ductal car

clinically effective differentiation therapy in acute myelogenous leukemia ( aml ) has been demonstrated only in the m3 t ( 15 ; 17 ) acute promyelocytic leukemia ( apl ) . in apl , all-retinoic acid ( atra ) induces leukemic cell terminal differentiation and hematologic remission in 90 % of patients . this remarkable clinical observation was initially based on the observation that retinoids induced terminal cell division in established leukemia cell lines . this biological observation and treatment of apl was made prior to the knowledge that dominant negative repression of rarα nuclear receptor function by pml rarα , the product of t ( 15 ; 17 ) , was the molecular basis for leukemic transformation in apl . the understanding of the molecular basis of the myeloid transformation to apl resulting from the pml rarα protein has brought forward a model for the development of novel strategies for overcoming the site-specific transcriptional repression involved in the transformation ( ) . rarα in heterodimeric form with rxr is associated with an n-cor / sin3a / histone deacetylase ( hdac1 ) corepressor complex . rarα is maintained in a repressed state when associated with the corepressor as a result of deacetylation of histone tails within the nucleosome resulting in less accessibility to basal transcription factors . during normal myeloid differentiation ( ) , physiologic concentrations of atra induce confirmational changes in the rarα causing dissociation of the corepressor complex with subsequent recruitment of an src co-activator complex with intrinsic histone acetyltransferase activity . the subsequent acetylation of histone tails disrupts the tightly packed and repressed chromatin structure allowing for access to the basal transcription factors and transcriptional activation . site-specific transcriptional repression by pml rarα protein results from inefficient dissociation of the n-cor repressor complex from the fusion protein at physiologic concentrations of atra ( ) . pharmacologic amounts of atra ( 1μ ) are required to dissociate the n-cor corepressor complex and initiate a chromatin structure amenable to transcriptional activation . other forms of acute leukemias are associated with translations which encode fusion leukemo

delim
dna double-strand breaks ( dsbs ) , which can arise from normal ( e . g . v ( d ) j and meiotic recombination ) and pathological ( stalled replication forks and reactive oxygen species ) endogenous metabolic processes or from exogenous agents ( e . g . ionizing radiation and radiomimetic drugs ) , are the most severe lesions with respect to cell survival and preservation of genomic integrity . therefore , cells have evolved complex mechanisms that include cell cycle arrest , activation and increased expression of various genes including those associated with dna repair and in certain cases induction of the apoptotic pathway , to respond to dsbs . the overall cellular response to dsbs has been considered as a classical signal-transduction cascade where the lesions ( signals ) are detected by sensor proteins that activate protein kinase ( transduction ) cascades , which result in amplification and diversification of the signal through a series of downstream effector molecules ( response ) . the central dsb signaling kinases in mammalian cells are ataxia telangiectasia mutated ( atm ) and ataxia telangiectasia-related ( also known as rad3-related , atr ) , which are members of the phosphoinositide 3-kinase ( pi ( 3 ) k ) superfamily . they catalyse the phosphorylation of numerous downstream substrates that are involved in cell-cycle regulation , dna repair and apoptosis . in mammalian cells , dsbs are repaired by one of two distinct and complementary pathways – homologous recombination ( hr ) and non-homologous end-joining ( nhej ) . briefly , nhej involves processing of the broken dna terminii to make them compatible , followed by a ligation step . the core components of nhej are the ku70 / ku80 heterodimer , which binds the broken dna ends , dna-dependent protein kinase catalytic subunit ( dna-pkcs ) , a pi ( 3 ) k member that activates and forms a complex with the nuclease artemis , and the xrcc4 / dna ligase iv complex , which ligates the processed dna terminii . recently , cernunnos-xlf , a protein that is defective in a rare inherited human syndrome characterized by severe immu

b cell acute lymphoblastic leukemia ( b-all ) is the most common form of childhood and adult all and is characterized by the clonal expansion in the bone marrow of neoplastic b cell precursors . current treatment is primarily based on combination chemotherapy . although most patients appear to be cured , survivors commonly develop morbidities that result from dose-intensified treatment with cytotoxic drugs . and , despite the use of aggressive salvage treatments , those who relapse have a dismal prognosis [ ] . the low long-term survival rate , particularly in adult patients , underscores the need for improved treatment . histone deacetylases inhibitors ( hdacis ) are emerging as a promising new class of anti-cancer agents , which have been proved to induce growth arrest , differentiation , and apoptosis in malignant cells [ , ] . in spite that many hdacis have been evaluated in clinical trials as single agents as well as in combination schemes in recent years [ ] , the pleiotropic effects and complicated molecular processes caused by structurally diverse hdacis still remain largely unknown . recently , hdacis were proved capable to inhibit proliferation and induce apoptosis in b-all cell lines [ – ] . the effects of hdacis in b-all cells as well as the underlying mechanisms , however , have not been fully elucidated . notch-1 is a member of a conserved family of closely related transmembrane receptors . members of the notch family receptors are activated upon ligand binding by a series of proteolytic cleavage events . on binding a ligand , the notch protein undergoes two proteolytic cleavages , translocates to the nucleus , where it forms a dna-binding complex with the centromere-binding factor ( cbf )-1 complex and alters transcription of target genes [ ] . the notch signaling pathway controls cell fate in multiple developmental programs and its dysregulation has been implicated in the oncogenesis of several types of cancer [ – ] . interestingly , notch signaling plays both oncogenic and tumor suppressor roles , depending on cell type [ ] . in contrast to t cell acute lymphoblastic leukemia ( all ) , where notch activation plays a key role in the leukemogenesis , induction of notch signaling in b-al

cancer has long been considered a disease caused by the accumulation of genetic mutations . in the last decade , however , several global proteomic and genomic technologies have led to the realization that genetic and epigenetic events cooperate in cancer development . epigenetic alterations cause deregulation in key biological targets and pathways involved in proliferation , differentiation , tumor suppression and oncogenicity ( hatziapostolou and iliopoulos ) , thus contributing to growth and progression in a variety of cancers . epigenetic modifications in chromatin involve dna methylation , posttranslational modifications of histones and mirna modulation as well as the positioning of nucleosomes along dna . histone modifications are dependent on multi-subunit complexes that perform “ writer , ” “ eraser ” and “ reader ” functions and act in a spatially and temporarily coordinated manner ( ruthenburg et al . ; taverna et al . ) . writer and eraser functions are carried out by subunits harboring catalytic activity that add or remove marks on histones , while the reader function often requires domains that specifically recognize and bind to these marks ( ruthenburg et al . ) . chromatin structure and chromatin accessibility for transcription factors and associated proteins are mediated by chromatin-regulating complexes , which act in a stepwise and / or combinatorial manner and engage in extensive cross talk . unlike static somatic mutations affecting dna , epigenetic aberrations are potentially reversible ( as are , for example , histone marks ) and / or can be restored through epigenetic therapy targeting overexpressed or mutated epi-targets ( conte and altucci ) . different drugs directed at epigenetic-modifying enzymes have been developed to block or reverse aberrant epigenetic modifications . these include histone acetyltransferases ( hats ) , dna methyltransferases ( dnmts ) , histone deacetylases ( hdacs ) , histone methyltransferases ( hmts ) and histone demethylases ( hdms ) . to date , some of these drugs ( e . g . , azacitidine , decitabine , vorinostat and romidepsin ) have been approved by the us food and drug administration ( fda ) for the treatment of various types of cancer and precancer

high mobility group box 1 ( hmgb1 ) is a 25-kda dna-binding protein that is overexpressed in various cancers . its expression is often associated with poor prognosis , higher tumor grade and metastasis . in a colon cancer study , hmgb1 was shown to be overexpressed in tumor tissue compared with adjacent normal tissue in 90 % of patients . in addition , a causative role for hmgb1 in promoting colon carcinogenesis was shown experimentally . similar results have been reported for hepatocellular carcinoma , nasopharyngeal carcinoma , prostate cancer , melanoma and breast cancer . the high prevalence of hmgb1 upregulation in diverse tumor types suggests a critical role in carcinogenesis ; however , despite a strong correlation between hmgb1 expression and negative clinical outcome , the mechanism by which hmgb1 promotes tumor growth and metastasis remains unclear . hmgb1 binds to dna without sequence specificity and aids in distorting the dna structure to allow access for repair and transcription proteins . hmgb1-deficient mice die within 24 h after birth from hypoglycemia as a result of defective glucocorticoid-mediated transcription . hmgb1 interacts with various transcription factors , including nfκb members , p53 and the tata-binding protein . interactions with these factors can promote or repress transcription depending on the cellular context . in addition to its roles in the nucleus , hmgb1 can also act as a ligand when released from dying or stressed cells . hmgb1 binds to the receptor for advanced glycation end products ( rage ) or toll-like receptors ( tlr ) 2 / 4 , which are expressed on many types of immune and tumor cells . hmgb1 binding to rage results in activation of the ras map kinase pathway and increased levels of phosphorylated p42 / 44 ( erk1 / 2 ) . the pro-tumor effects of hmgb1 are often attributed to its extracellular role , through stimulation of the mapk pathway via rage binding . functionally , preventing extracellular release of hmgb1 by drug treatment or blocking hmgb1 signaling with antibodies can reduce tumor growth and metastasis in some experimental models of cancer . in addition , rage-deficient mice are resistant to tumor formation in chemical carcinogen-induced skin cancer

delim
transcription of individual genes can be altered in cancer by genetic but also epigenetic lesions . focal promoter dna methylation can , for example , modify gene expression . however , studying the regulation of genes in isolation without taking into account their genomic context limits the understanding of regulatory networks in cancer . many clusters of co-regulated genes have been reported in mammalian genomes , such as the hox clusters or the classical major histocompatibility complex . the regulation of these genomic regions is complex and can result from the interaction of multiple factors including epigenetic modifications , chromatin conformation and nuclear localization , non coding rnas or polycomb complexes . prc2 and prc1 polycomb complexes take part in the delineation and regulation of gene clusters , such as the hox or kcnoqt1 clusters , notably through the deposition of h3k27me3 and chromatin compaction mechanisms . several studies have addressed the existence of co-regulated gene clusters specific to cancer cells . regions of expression bias , where genes are coordinately deregulated in tumors compared with normal tissue , have been reported in various tumor types using large-scale expression data sets . many of these regions were attributable to known dna copy-number alterations , however , a significant portion of them are independent of such genetic alterations . moreover , it has been reported that epigenetic alterations , such as histone modifications with or without aberrant dna methylation , can affect several neighboring genes in cancer and correspond to the formation of clusters of corepressed genes . recently , we and others showed that regional epigenetic silencing is frequent in bladder and prostate cancer . however , little is known about the mechanisms underlying this novel epigenetic alteration . we previously reported in bladder cancer that regional epigenetic silencing occurs in a particularly aggressive group of tumors , the tumors of the carcinoma

delim
in a severe stressful situation , the levels of circulating glucocorticoids rise . if such a stressful situation occurs during pregnancy , glucocorticoids pass through the placenta and affect fetus normal development . during prenatal stress ( ps ) , glucocorticoids reach the brain and modify gene expression triggering cellular , physiological , and behavioral changes ( van den hove et al . ; baier et al . ) . in particular , hippocampal neurons from offspring of stressed mothers are negatively affected by ps ( mychasiuk et al . ) showing reduced neurogenesis ( lemaire et al . ) , decreased dendritic tree size ( hosseini-sharifabad and hadinedoushan ) , and diminished synaptic density ( hayashi et al . ) . in addition , there is a change in the expression of many genes linked to neuronal plasticity such as neurotrophic factors , neurotransmitter receptors , and synaptic proteins ( fumagalli et al . , ; van den hove et al . ; revest et al . ; baier et al . ; pallarés et al . ; monteleone et al . ; adrover et al . ) . retrospective studies on children born from stressed mothers show as attention-deficit hyperactivity disorder ( adhd ) and sleep disturbance during infancy ( beydoun and saftlas ) . for that reason , ps represents one of the main risk factors for affective disorders ( van den bergh et al . ; glover ; baier et al . ) . in response to environmental stimuli , stress-induced genetic and epigenetic changes steer neuronal remodeling , a type of neuronal plasticity . plasticity involves changes in gene expression and in the neuron ’ s structure , function , and organization that underlie many key brain processes . the stress-induced structural alterations result in functional disconnections that may underlie the neuropsychiatric disease pathophysiology but might also include clues for treatment . neural connectivity is modulated by plasticity-related genes whose expression is controlled by different transcription factors . among them , the serum response factor ( srf ) and the yin yang 1 ( yy1 ) factor have been related to chronic stress . srf promotes resilience to chronic social stress ( vialou et al . ) and yy1 participates in anxiety

the chromatin remodeler swi / snf harbors a large number of subunits ( 12 genes in yeast , 29 in human ; see [ ] for review ; fig . a ) , whose functions are conserved among eukaryotes [ ] . early work identified swi / snf as a transcription activator through histones sliding and alteration of the nucleosome structure [ ] . since then , it has been implicated in dna replication , damage repair , apoptosis , metabolism , and cell differentiation . mutations or aberrant expression of swi / snf subunits are frequently found in a broad range of cancer subtypes [ ] , hinting at subtle and tissue-specific regulation of the swi / snf subunits . contribution of individual swi / snf subunits to the complex function and its structure stability have been extensively studied in yeast [ , ] and humans [ ] . these studies have provided insights into how mutations in individual subunits or their epigenetic silencing affect gene expression and favor carcinogenesis [ – ] . the catalytic subunits , brg1 or brm , are essential for enzymatic function and the structural integrity of swi / snf , and have been intensely studied . in contrast , tissue-specific subunits ( brg1 associated factors , or baf ) and non-catalytic subunits of swi / snf , e . g . , smarcd3 , one of three paralogs of smarcd ( , or baf60a / b / c , respectively ) , remain poorly characterized . smarcd1 / 2 / 3 are mutually exclusive , tissue-specific , and their function is only partially redundant as they cannot complement each other [ , ] . they have been identified as recruiter of the swi / snf complex to target site on the chromatin through interaction with protein partners [ , ] . smarcd1 / 2 role in the complex have been better characterized ad smarcd3 precise function remains to be discovered . however , previous work smarcd3 shed light on smarcd3 as a potentially essential subunit . for instance , smarcd3 is critical for cell differentiation via direct interactions with partners such as myod , thus coordinating cell differentiation cascades through transcriptional activation of genes , and through epigenetic reprogramming [ , ] . recent studies have associated smarcd3 levels and breast

delim
gut microbiota is designated as “ the fellow travelers , ” as they are the permanent residents of our gastrointestinal tract ( git ) . the gut microbiome constitutes a variety of different microorganisms , which include several species of viruses , bacteria , protozoa , and fungi . this microbiome shows vast diversity amongst different population groups and has a significant influence on human health , disease state , and overall well-being ( zmora et al . ) . the number of gut microbes within the git is estimated to be approximately 100 trillion , which is 10 times the number of cells found in the human body . the gut microbiome is about 150 times greater than that of the human genome and encodes 100-fold more unique genes than our genome , which suggests their vast possibilities in influencing human health . extensive research in the recent past has suggested a direct association of gut microbiota with a variety of disorders including diabetes mellitus , atherosclerosis , hypertension , heart disorders , cardiovascular complications , and cns disorders such as alzheimer ’ s disease ( ad ) or parkinsonism . the gut microbiota has been found to modulate the pathogenesis of several neurodegenerative disorders ; however , the exact mechanism involved is yet to be discovered ( bonfili et al . ) . ad is one of the most prevalent irreversible neurodegenerative disorders resulting in progressive dementia . ad patients show short-term memory loss , neuronal hypotrophy , impaired coordination capabilities , aggregation of amyloid-β ( aβ ) peptides , accumulation of extracellular amyloidal plaques and neurofibrillary tangles , synaptic dysfunction , impaired synaptic plasticity , neurodegeneration , and neuroinflammation ( mir et al . ; skaper et al . ) . accumulated evidence suggests that dysbiosis leads to the destruction of the intestinal barrier and results in increased intestinal permeability . this leads to increased systemic concentration of inflammatory mediators such as cytokines and bacterial metabolites , which in turn may impair the integrity of the blood – brain barrier ( bbb ) and promote neuroinflammation and neurodegeneration , thereby contributing to the development and progression of cns disorders such as ad
